<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_dress_code">Western dress code</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Western dress code">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_dress_code" title="Western dress code">Western dress code</a></div>
<p>The Western dress code has changed over the past 500+ years. The mechanization of the <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textile industry</a> made many varieties of cloth widely available at affordable prices.  Styles have changed, and the availability of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synthetic_fabric" title="Synthetic fabric">synthetic fabrics</a> has changed the definition of what is "stylish". In the latter half of the twentieth century, <a href="/wiki/Jeans" title="Jeans">blue jeans</a> became very popular, and are now worn to events that normally demand formal attire. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Activewear" title="Activewear">Activewear</a> has also become a large and growing market.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2030" data-file-width="1624" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png/220px-GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png/330px-GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png/440px-GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GuyLaroche_suit_jacket_83d40m_black_skirt_late1959_early1960_vintage.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jacket by Guy Laroche, from a woman's suit with a black skirt and blouse (1960)</div></div></div>
<p>In the Western dress code, jeans are worn by both men and women. There are several unique styles of jeans found that include: high rise jeans, mid rise jeans, low rise jeans, bootcut jeans, straight jeans, cropped jeans, skinny jeans, cuffed jeans, boyfriend jeans, and capri jeans.
</p><p>The licensing of designer names was pioneered by designers such as <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Cardin" title="Pierre Cardin">Pierre Cardin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yves_Saint_Laurent_(designer)" title="Yves Saint Laurent (designer)">Yves Saint Laurent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guy_Laroche" title="Guy Laroche">Guy Laroche</a> in the 1960s and has been a common practice within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fashion_industry" title="Fashion industry">fashion industry</a> from about the 1970s. Among the more popular include <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a>, named for Marc Jacobs and Guccio Gucci respectively.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spread_of_western_styles">Spread of western styles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Spread of western styles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Move_In_Day_2011_(6099706937)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1832" data-file-width="2470" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Move_In_Day_2011_%286099706937%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Move_In_Day_2011_(6099706937)_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University students in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casual_clothes" title="Casual clothes">casual clothes</a> in the U.S.</div></div></div>
<p>By the early years of the twenty-first century, western clothing styles had, to some extent, become international styles. This process began hundreds of years earlier, during the periods of European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>. The process of cultural dissemination has been perpetuated over the centuries, spreading Western culture and styles, most recently as Western media corporations have penetrated markets throughout the world. <a href="/wiki/Fast_fashion" title="Fast fashion">Fast fashion</a> clothing has also become a global phenomenon. These garments are less expensive, mass-produced Western clothing. Also, donated <a href="/wiki/Used_good" title="Used good">used</a> clothing from Western countries is delivered to people in poor countries by charity organizations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_and_cultural_heritage">Ethnic and cultural heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ethnic and cultural heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>People may wear ethnic or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_costume" title="National costume">national dress</a> on special occasions or in certain roles or occupations. For example, most Korean men and women have adopted Western-style dress for daily wear, but still wear traditional <a href="/wiki/Hanbok" title="Hanbok">hanboks</a> on special occasions, such as weddings and cultural holidays. Also, items of <a href="/wiki/Western_wear" title="Western wear">Western dress</a> may be worn or accessorized in distinctive, non-Western ways. A Tongan man may combine a used <a href="/wiki/T-shirt" title="T-shirt">T-shirt</a> with a Tongan wrapped skirt, or <a href="/wiki/Tupenu" title="Tupenu">tupenu</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport_and_activity">Sport and activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sport and activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Activewear" title="Activewear">Activewear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sportswear_(fashion)" title="Sportswear (fashion)">Sportswear (fashion)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_(6635665267)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1861" data-file-width="1860" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_%286635665267%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Keeping_Fit_and_Connected_(6635665267)_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A woman wearing <a href="/wiki/Sports_bra" title="Sports bra">sports bra</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boyshorts" title="Boyshorts">boyshorts</a>, conventionally women's <a href="/wiki/Sportswear" title="Sportswear">sportswear</a>, but now worn as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casual_attire" title="Casual attire">casuals</a> or <a href="/wiki/Athleisure" title="Athleisure">athleisure</a> by women in the West</div></div></div>
<p>For practical, comfort or safety reasons most sports and physical activities are practiced wearing special clothing. Common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportswear_(activewear)" title="Sportswear (activewear)">sportswear</a> garments include <a href="/wiki/Shorts" title="Shorts">shorts</a>, <a href="/wiki/T-shirt" title="T-shirt">T-shirts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tennis_shirt" title="Tennis shirt">tennis shirts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leotard" title="Leotard">leotards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracksuit" title="Tracksuit">tracksuits</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletic_shoe" title="Athletic shoe">trainers</a>. Specialized garments include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wet_suit" title="Wet suit">wet suits</a> (for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_swimming" title="Human swimming">swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_diving" title="Underwater diving">diving</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salopettes" title="Salopettes">salopettes</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leotards" title="Leotards">leotards</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a>). Also, <a href="/wiki/Spandex" title="Spandex">spandex</a> materials often are used as base layers to soak up sweat. Spandex is preferable for active sports that require form fitting garments, such as volleyball, wrestling, <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, dance, gymnastics, and swimming.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:E1275480_(4315537281).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3551" data-file-width="2366" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg/170px-E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg/255px-E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg/340px-E1275480_%284315537281%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:E1275480_(4315537281).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fashion_show" title="Fashion show">Fashion shows</a> often are the source of the latest trends in clothing <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashions</a>, photograph of a <a href="/wiki/Model_(person)" title="Model (person)">model</a> in a modern <a href="/wiki/Gown" title="Gown">gown</a> reflecting the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fashion_trend" title="Fashion trend">fashion trend</a> at an <a href="/wiki/Haute_couture" title="Haute couture">Haute couture</a> fashion show</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">Fashion</a> and <a href="/wiki/2020s_in_fashion" title="2020s in fashion">2020s in fashion</a></div>
<p>Paris set the 1900–1940 fashion trends for Europe and North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In the 1920s the goal was all about getting loose. Women wore dresses all day, every day. Day dresses had a drop waist, which was a sash or belt around the low waist or hip and a skirt that hung anywhere from the ankle on up to the knee, never above. Daywear had sleeves (long to mid-bicep) and a skirt that was straight, pleated, hank hemmed, or tiered. Jewelry was not conspicuous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>  Hair was often bobbed, giving a boyish look.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early twenty-first century a diverse range of styles exists in fashion, varying by geography, exposure to modern media, economic conditions, and ranging from expensive <a href="/wiki/Haute_couture" title="Haute couture">haute couture</a>, to traditional garb, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thrift_store" title="Thrift store">thrift store</a> <a href="/wiki/Grunge" title="Grunge">grunge</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fashion_show" title="Fashion show">Fashion shows</a> are events for designers to show off new and often extravagant designs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_issues">Political issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Political issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_conditions_in_the_garments_industry">Working conditions in the garments industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Working conditions in the garments industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garment_industry" title="Garment industry">Garment industry</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="565" data-file-width="753" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG/220px-Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG/330px-Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG/440px-Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Garments_Factory_in_Bangladesh.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Garments factory in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left,_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right,_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2944" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg/170px-Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg/255px-Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg/340px-Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left%2C_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right%2C_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Safety_garb_for_women_workers._The_uniform_at_the_left,_complete_with_the_plastic_%22bra%22_on_the_right,_will_prevent..._-_NARA_-_522882.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Safety garb for women was designed to prevent occupational accidents among war workers, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> display (c. 1943)</div></div></div>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Mechanization" title="Mechanization">mechanization</a> transformed most aspects of human <a href="/wiki/Clothing_industry" title="Clothing industry">clothing industry</a> by the mid-twentieth century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garment" title="Garment">garment</a> workers have continued to labor under challenging conditions that demand repetitive manual labor. Often, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass-produced" title="Mass-produced">mass-produced</a> clothing is made in what are considered by some to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweatshops" title="Sweatshops">sweatshops</a>, typified by long work hours, lack of benefits, and lack of worker representation. While most examples of such conditions are found in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>, clothes made in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialized_nation" title="Industrialized nation">industrialized nations</a> may also be manufactured under similar conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>Coalitions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">NGOs</a>, designers (including Katharine Hamnett, <a href="/wiki/American_Apparel" title="American Apparel">American Apparel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veja_Sneakers" title="Veja Sneakers">Veja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quiksilver" title="Quiksilver">Quiksilver</a>, eVocal, and Edun), and campaign groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Clothes_Campaign" title="Clean Clothes Campaign">Clean Clothes Campaign</a> (CCC) and the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Global_Labour_and_Human_Rights" title="Institute for Global Labour and Human Rights">Institute for Global Labour and Human Rights</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Textile_and_clothing_trade_unions" title="Textile and clothing trade unions">textile and clothing trade unions</a> have sought to improve these conditions by sponsoring awareness-raising events, which draw the attention of both the media and the general public to the plight of the workers.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">Outsourcing</a> production to low wage countries such as <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> became possible when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi_Fibre_Agreement" title="Multi Fibre Agreement">Multi Fibre Agreement</a> (MFA) was abolished. The MFA, which placed quotas on textiles imports, was deemed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protectionist" title="Protectionist">protectionist</a> measure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although many countries recognize treaties such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a>, which attempt to set standards for worker safety and rights, many countries have made exceptions to certain parts of the treaties or failed to thoroughly enforce them. India for example has not ratified sections 87 and 92 of the treaty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">production of textiles</a> has functioned as a consistent industry for developing nations, providing work and wages, whether construed as exploitative or not, to millions of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fur">Fur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Fur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fur_clothing" title="Fur clothing">Fur clothing</a></div>
<p>The use of animal fur in clothing dates to prehistoric times. Currently, although fur is still used by indigenous people in arctic zones and higher elevations for its warmth and protection, in developed countries it is associated with expensive, designer clothing. Once uncontroversial, recently it has been the focus of campaigns on the grounds that campaigners consider it cruel and unnecessary. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA">PETA</a>, along with other <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_liberation_movement" title="Animal liberation movement">animal liberation</a> groups have called attention to <a href="/wiki/Fur_farming" title="Fur farming">fur farming</a> and other practices they consider cruel.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_cycle">Life cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Life cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clothing_maintenance">Clothing maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Clothing maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Clothing suffers assault both from within and without. The human body sheds skin cells and body oils, and it exudes sweat, urine, and feces that may soil clothing. From the outside, sun damage, moisture, abrasion, and dirt assault garments. Fleas and lice can hide in seams. If not cleaned and refurbished, clothing becomes worn and loses its <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics_(textile)" title="Aesthetics (textile)">aesthetics</a> and functionality (as when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Button_(clothing)" title="Button (clothing)">buttons</a> fall off, seams come undone, fabrics thin or tear, and <a href="/wiki/Zipper" title="Zipper">zippers</a> fail).
</p><p>Often, people wear an item of clothing until it falls apart. Some materials present problems. Cleaning leather is difficult, and bark cloth (tapa) cannot be washed without dissolving it. Owners may patch tears and rips, and brush off surface dirt, but materials such as these inevitably age.
</p><p>Most clothing consists of cloth, however, and most cloth can be <a href="/wiki/Laundry" title="Laundry">laundered</a> and mended (patching, <a href="/wiki/Darning" title="Darning">darning</a>, but compare <a href="/wiki/Felt" title="Felt">felt</a>).
</p>
<h3><span id="Laundry.2C_ironing.2C_storage"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Laundry,_ironing,_storage">Laundry, ironing, storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Laundry, ironing, storage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat,_Walden,_NY.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3732" data-file-width="4536" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg/220px-Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg/330px-Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg/440px-Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat%2C_Walden%2C_NY.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Washers_in_Sheeley%27s_Laundromat,_Walden,_NY.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laundromat" title="Laundromat">Laundromat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Walden,_New_York" title="Walden, New York">Walden, New York</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<p>Humans have developed many specialized methods for laundering clothing, ranging from early methods of pounding clothes against rocks in running streams, to the latest in electronic <a href="/wiki/Washing_machine" title="Washing machine">washing machines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dry_cleaning" title="Dry cleaning">dry cleaning</a> (dissolving dirt in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solvents" title="Solvents">solvents</a> other than water). Hot water washing (boiling), chemical cleaning, and ironing are all traditional methods of <a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(microbiology)" title="Sterilization (microbiology)">sterilizing</a> fabrics for <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a> purposes.
</p><p>Many kinds of clothing are designed to be <a href="/wiki/Ironing" title="Ironing">ironed</a> before they are worn to remove wrinkles. Most modern formal and semi-formal clothing is in this category (for example, <a href="/wiki/Dress_shirt" title="Dress shirt">dress shirts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suit_(clothing)" title="Suit (clothing)">suits</a>). Ironed clothes are believed to look clean, fresh, and neat. Much contemporary casual clothing is made of knit materials that do not readily wrinkle, and do not require ironing. Some clothing is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_press" title="Permanent press">permanent press</a>, having been treated with a coating (such as <a href="/wiki/Polytetrafluoroethylene" title="Polytetrafluoroethylene">polytetrafluoroethylene</a>) that suppresses wrinkles and creates a smooth appearance without ironing. Excess lint or debris may end up on the clothing in between launderings. In such cases, a <a href="/wiki/Lint_remover" title="Lint remover">lint remover</a> may be useful.
</p><p>Once clothes have been laundered and possibly ironed, usually they are hung on <a href="/wiki/Clothes_hanger" title="Clothes hanger">clothes hangers</a> or folded, to keep them fresh until they are worn. Clothes are folded to allow them to be stored compactly, to prevent creasing, to preserve creases, or to present them in a more pleasing manner, for instance, when they are put on sale in stores.
</p><p>Certain types of insects and larvae feed on clothing and textiles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Black_carpet_beetle" title="Black carpet beetle">black carpet beetle</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clothing_Moth" title="Clothing Moth">clothing moths</a>. To deter such pests, clothes may be stored in cedar-lined closets or chests,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> or placed in drawers or containers with materials having pest repellent properties, such as <a href="/wiki/Lavandula#Other_uses" title="Lavandula">lavender</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mothball" title="Mothball">mothballs</a>. Airtight containers (such as sealed, heavy-duty plastic bags) may deter insect pest damage to clothing materials as well.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-iron">Non-iron</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Non-iron">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_press" title="Permanent press">Permanent press</a></div>
<p>A resin used for making non-wrinkle shirts releases <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">formaldehyde</a>, which could cause contact dermatitis for some people; no disclosure requirements exist, and in 2008 the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office" title="Government Accountability Office">Government Accountability Office</a> tested formaldehyde in clothing and found that generally the highest levels were in non-wrinkle shirts and pants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In 1999, a study of the effect of washing on the formaldehyde levels found that after six months of routine washing, 7 of 27 shirts still had levels in excess of 75 ppm (the safe limit for direct skin exposure).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mending">Mending</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mending">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the raw material – cloth – was worth more than labor, it made sense to expend labor in saving it. In past times, mending was an art. A meticulous <a href="/wiki/Tailor" title="Tailor">tailor</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seamstress" title="Seamstress">seamstress</a> could mend rips with thread raveled from <a href="/wiki/Hem" title="Hem">hems</a> and seam edges so skillfully that the tear was practically invisible. Today clothing is considered a consumable item. Mass-manufactured clothing is less expensive than the labor required to repair it. Many people buy a new piece of clothing rather than spend time mending. The thrifty still replace <a href="/wiki/Zipper" title="Zipper">zippers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Button_(clothing)" title="Button (clothing)">buttons</a> and sew up ripped hems, however. Other mending techniques include <a href="/wiki/Darning" title="Darning">darning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invisible_mending" title="Invisible mending">invisible mending</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recycling">Recycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Recycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_(Canada)_munitions_factory_(I0004928).tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2930" data-file-width="3700" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_%28Canada%29_munitions_factory_%28I0004928%29.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clothing_salvage_centre_at_the_General_Engineering_Company_(Canada)_munitions_factory_(I0004928).tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clothing salvage centre at the General Engineering Company (Canada) munitions factory during the Second World War</div></div></div>
<p>It is estimated that 80 billion to 150 billion garments are produced annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Used, unwearable clothing can be repurposed for <a href="/wiki/Quilt" title="Quilt">quilts</a>, <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rag" title="wikt:rag">rags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carpet" title="Carpet">rugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bandage" title="Bandage">bandages</a>, and many other household uses. Neutral colored or undyed <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a> fibers can be recycled into <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">paper</a>. In Western societies, used clothing is often thrown out or donated to charity (such as through a <a href="/wiki/Clothing_bin" title="Clothing bin">clothing bin</a>). It is also sold to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consignment_shop" title="Consignment shop">consignment shops</a>, dress agencies, <a href="/wiki/Flea_market" title="Flea market">flea markets</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Online_auction" title="Online auction">online auctions</a>. Also, used clothing often is collected on an industrial scale to be sorted and shipped for re-use in poorer countries. Globally, used clothes are worth $4 billion, with the U.S. as the leading exporter at $575 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Synthetics, which come primarily from petrochemicals, are not renewable or biodegradable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Excess inventory of clothing is sometimes destroyed to preserve brand value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_trade">Global trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clothing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Global trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>EU Member States import, in 2018 €166 billion of clothes; 51% come from outside the EU €84 billion.
</p><p>EU member states exported €116 billion of clothes in 2018, including 77% to other EU member states.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFGaggeStolwijkHardy1967">Gagge, A.P.; Stolwijk, J.A.J.; Hardy, J.D. (1967-06-01). <a class="external text" href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/0013935167900023" rel="nofollow">"Comfort and thermal sensations and associated physiological responses at various ambient temperatures"</a>. <i>Environmental Research</i>. <b>1</b> (1): 1–20. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1967ER......1....1G" rel="nofollow">1967ER......1....1G</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2F0013-9351%2867%2990002-3" rel="nofollow">10.1016/0013-9351(67)90002-3</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0013-9351" rel="nofollow">0013-9351</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/5614624" rel="nofollow">5614624</a>. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210719032305/https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/0013935167900023" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 2021-07-19<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-07-17</span></span>. <q><i>For steady exposure to cold and warm environments, thermal comfort and neutral temperature sensations lie in the range for physiological thermal neutrality (28°–30°C), in which there is no physiological temperature regulatory effort. Discomfort increases more rapidly below 28°C than above 30°C, while thermal sensation for both heat and cold increases rapidly each side of neutral. Discomfort correlates best with lowering average skin temperature toward cold environments and with increased sweating toward hot environments. In general, discomfort is associated with a change of average body temperature from 36.5°C.</i></q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Environmental+Research&amp;rft.atitle=Comfort+and+thermal+sensations+and+associated+physiological+responses+at+various+ambient+temperatures&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=1-20&amp;rft.date=1967-06-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2F0013-9351%2867%2990002-3&amp;rft.issn=0013-9351&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F5614624&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1967ER......1....1G&amp;rft.aulast=Gagge&amp;rft.aufirst=A.P.&amp;rft.au=Stolwijk%2C+J.A.J.&amp;rft.au=Hardy%2C+J.D.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.sciencedirect.com%2Fscience%2Farticle%2Fabs%2Fpii%2F0013935167900023&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AClothing"></span></span>
</li>
